Promethazine tablets What is this medicine?

PROMETHAZINE (proe METH a zeen) is an antihistamine. It is used to treat allergic reactions and to treat or prevent nausea and vomiting from iHiness or motion sickness. [t is aiso used to make you sleep before surgery, and to help treat pain or nausea after surgery.

How should I use this medicine?

Take this medicine by mouth with a glass of water. Follow the directions on the prescription label, Take your doses at regular intervals. Do not take your medicine more often than directed.

Talk to your pediatrician regarding the use of this medicine in children. Special care may be needed. This medicine should not be given to infants and children younger than 2 years old.

What side effects may I notice from receiving this medicine? Side effects that you should report to your doctor or health care professional as soon as possible:

® blared vision

* irregular heartbeat, palpitations or chest pain ® muscle or facial twitches

@ pain or difficulty passing urine

® seizures

® skin rash

® slowed or shallow breathing

* unusual bleeding or bruising

® yellowing of the eyes or skin

Side effects that usually do not require medical attention {report to your doctor or health care professional if they continue or are bothersome}:

@ headache

* nightmares, agitation, Nervousness, excitability, not able to sleep (these are more likely in children}

* stuffy nose

What may interact with this medicine?

(Do not take this medicine with any of the following meclications:

* cisapride

® dofetilide

* dronedarone

@ MAOIs tike Carbex, Eldepryl, Marplan, Nerdil, Parnate ®@ pimozide

® quinidine, including dextromethorphan; quinkline




Page 2 of 3

Name: Cora Mae Mail

Acet Nuri: LOOOS@4Q 7077

Med Rec Nunn LOOOGT7236 Locations BGM Ambulatory Surge

Primary Provider: Malempali, Chaitanya S Dabe: 1248/22

® thioridazine @ ziprasikione

This medicine may also interact with the following medications:

® certain medicines for depression, anxiety, or psychotic disturbances

* certain medicines for anxiety or sleep

# certain medicines for seizures like carbamazepine, phenobarbital, phenytoin

@ certain medicines for movement abnormalities as in Parkinson's disease, or for gastrointestinal problems

* epinephrine

® medicines for allergies or colds

@ muscle relaxants

* narcotic medicines for pain

* other medicines that prolong the OT interval (cause an abnormal heart rhythm)

® tramadol

® trimethobenzamide

What if I miss a dase?

Tf you miss a dose, take it as soon as you can. If it is almost time for your next dose, take only that dose. Do not take double or extra doses.

Where should I keep my medicine? Keep out of the reach of children.

Store at room temperature, between 20 and 25 degrees {68 and 7? degrees F). Protect from light. Throw away any unused medicine after the expiration date.

What should I tell my health care provider before I take this medicine? They need to know if you have any of these conditions:

@ glaucoma

&@ high blood pressure or heart disease

@ kidney disease

@ liver disease

@ lung or breathing disease, like asthma

* prostate trouble

@ pain or difficulty passing urine

* seizures

* an unusual or allergic reaction to promethazine or phenothiazines, other medicines, foods, dyes, or preservatives

* pregnant or trying to get pregnant

* breast-feeding

What should I watch for while using this medicine?

Name: Cora Mae Mail

Acet Nuri: LOOOS@4Q 7077

Med Rec Nunn LOOOGT7236 Locations BGM Ambulatory Surge

Primary Provider: Malempali, Chaitanya S Dabe: 1248/22

Tell your dactor or health care professional if your symptoms do not start to get better in 1 ta 2 days.

You may get drowsy or dizzy. Do not drive, use machinery, or do anything that needs mental alertness until you know bow this medicine affects you. To reduce the risk of dizzy or fainting spells, do not stand or sit up quickly, especially if you are an older patient, Alcohol may increase dizziness and drowsiness. Avoid alcoholic drinks.

Your mouth may get dry. Chewing sugariess gurn or sucking herd candy, and drinking plenty of water may help. Contact your doctor if the problem does not go away or is severe.

This medicine may cause dry eyes and blurred vision. If you wear contact lenses you may fee! some discomfort. Lubricating drops may help. See your eye doctor if the problem does not go away or is severe,

This medicine can make you more sensitive to the sun. Keep out of the sun. If you cannot avoid being in the sun, wear protective clothing and use sunscreen. Do not use sun lamps or tanning beds/booths.

If you are diabetic, check your blood-sugar levels regularly,

Norco Oral Tablet 10 mg/325 mg Uses

For pain.

Instructions

This medicine may be taken with or without food.

Keep the medicine at room temperature. Avoid heat and direct light.

To reduce constipation, eat high Aber foods, drink plenty of water and exercise.

Please tell your doctor and pharmacist about all the medicines you take. Include both prescription and over-the-counter medicines. Also tell them about any vitamins, herbal medicines, or anything else you take for your health.

Tt is very important that you follow your doctor's instructions for all blood tests.

Do not take more than 6 pills in a day.

Cautions

This medicine contains an opioid. Though it helps many people, this medicine may sometimes cause addiction, especially if it is used for a lang time. This risk for addiction may be higher if you have a substance use disorder - such as overuse of or addiction to drugs or aicohol. Speak with your doctor about the benefits and risks of using this medicine.

Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you should have naloxone on hand to treat opioid overdose. Teach your farnily or household members about the signs of an opioid overdose and how to treat it,

if you stop this medicine suddeniy, after using it reqularly for a long time, you may have withdrawal symptoms. Your doctor may ask you to slowly reduce your dose before stopping it. Tel your doctor right away if you notice any symptoms of withdrawal. Withdrawal symptoms can include unusual sweating, watering eyes, runny nose, chills, stomach pain, diarrhea, yawning, muscle aches, initability, restlessness, anxiety, trouble sleeping, or thoughts of suicide.

Tell your doctor and pharmacist if you ever had an allergic reaction to a medicine. Symptoms of an allergic reaction can include trouble breathing, skin rash, itching, swelling, or severe dizziness.

Do not use the medication any more than instructed.

If possible, avoid using with marijuana or other medicines that can cause dizziness or drowsiness. These include allergy/cold products, muscle relaxers, sieep aids, and pain relievers.

Your abllity to stay alert or to react quickly may be impaired by this medicine. Do not operate

machinery or drive while on this medicine.

Do not drink beverages with alcohal while on this medicine. Yell the doctor or pharmacist if you are pregnant, planning to be pregnant, or breastfeeding.

This medicine can hurt a new baby in the wornb. If you become pregnant while on this medicina, tell your doctor immediately. Your doctor may switch you to a different medicine.

Ask your pharmacist if this medicine can interact with any of your other medicines. Be sure to tell them about all the medicines you take.

Please tell all your doctors and dentists that you are on this medicine before they provide care. Oo not start or stop any other medicines without first speaking to your doctor or pharmacist. This medicine should be used with caution in patients with breathing difficulties.

Call your doctor right away if you notice slow or shallow breathing.

Do not share this medicine with anyone who has not been prescribed this medicine.

This medicine contains acetaminophen. There are many medicines with acetaminophen. Taking these medicines together can cause you to get too much acetaminophen. This can cause serious liver problerns. Look carefully on the package of all your medicines to see if acetarninaphen Is included. Ask your pharmacist which medicines you can take safely.

Bladder Care after Outpatient Surgery Caring for your Bladder after Outpatient Surgery

Sometimes surgery and anesthesia medicines can affect your bladder for several hours. This information will help you care for your bladder after you are discharged home. The inability to empty your bladder after surgery, a condition called urinary retention, is considered an emergency if you are no fonger in the hospital. If you are unable to empty your bladder within 6-8 hours from the time your surgery ended, you should seek treatment from your focal emergency room. This time is 0 afore.

How does surgery affect my bladder?

» Surgery can cause a ternporary interruption of nerve impulses from the brain to the bladder, decreasing the sensation and feeling that you need to urinate.

« Temporary swelling after surgery can alse affect your ability to empty your bladder.

+ When the bladder gets full and can hold no more urine, it can cause stretching of the bladder which can cause damage to the bladder muscles. When the bladder can hold no more urine, fluid backs up inte the kidneys, which can also cause damage.

What can I do if 1 can’t urinate?

: Try running the water in the sink. Sometimes the sound of running water helps.

» Sit in a warm bath or get inte the shower (if not contraindicated by your procedure}.

+ Try placing your hands in cold water.

» Walk, Walk. Walk.

» Do not keep drinking large arnounts of fluid if you feel Hke your bladder is full and you cannot empty tt.

* GO TO YOUR LOCAL EMERGENCY ROOM

‘The doctor has explained to me: (1) the nature, purpose, description and benefits of the operation, special procedure or treatment; (2) the possibility that complications may arise or develop during the procedure or treatment or recuperation period, and the risks which may be involved, (3) the likelihood of achieving treatment goals; and (4} the possible alternative methods of treatment, along with the benefits, risks and side effects associated with the alternatives, including not having the procedure or treatment performed. |

I authorize and direct my doctor(s) and associates gr assistants, any healthcare provider or healthcare provider in training and The Medical Center to provide such additional services as they deem necessary, including, but not limited to, the administration or maintenance of anesthesia (including sedation , analgesia), and the performance of services involving pathology and radiology. Iunderstand medical | services may be performed by physicians or other persons who are not egents or employees of The | Medical Center, but are independent contractors, fe I may be billed separately for their services.

T understand there are inherent risks with the administration of anesthesia. The doctor, anesthesiologist, , nurse anesthetist or nurse practitioner has explained the risks, benefits and alternative methods of | anesthesia. Complications associated with all types of anesthesia include, but are not limited to, damage | to teeth, lips, nose, throat, voice box, windpipe, eyes, nerves or blood vessels. Drag reactions can occur | | and may be minor or serious. Very serious complications, including paralysis, brain damage or death are uncommon, but can occur. :

Any tissue, organ, extremity or other body part surgically removed may be disposed of by The Medical Center in accordance with its usual practice.

Some procedures may require a transfusion of blood or blood products. I understand a blood transfusion is when blood or blood products are given through a sterile needle into one of my veins. I have been informed of the benefits, alternatives and risks involved in receiving a blood transfusion. The possible risks include, but are not limited to, reactions such as: bruising, swelling, infection or bleeding at the needle site; headache, fever, itching or arash; volume overload which could affect the heart or lungs;

_ and rarely, transmission of diseases such as HIV, AIDS and hepatitis, which require lengthy treatment and can be fatal. (Although the procedures for screening blood products for diseases such as HIV, AIDS and hepatitis are effective, no process or testing is 100% reliable.)

Madical PREOPERATIVE PREGNANCY TESTING Center Education, Consent and/or Refusal of Testing

BOVTLING GREEN « SCOTTSVILLE « HNN

This is to educate female patients within childbearing yearg undergoing surgery of the potential dangers of anesthesia on a fetus. Exposure to anesthestic agents within the first mn (first 3 months) of pregnancy may have possible = ’ effects on the fetus. ‘

4 s Studies from the American Society of Anesthesiclogists, the Centers for Disease Control and others differ on their | analysis & findings. However, studies have shown there may be a possibility of an increase in hydrocephalus (an incrdase in cerebrospinal fluid in the ventricles of the brain), a possible increase chance of neuro tubal defect (a defect effecting spinal cord and brain) and other effects (malformations) that can occur when the fetus has been exposed to certain anesthestic agents in the first trimester. Also, there could be spontaneous abortion or possible stillbirth.

Ambulatory Surgery and The Anesthesia Department are providing this information to you so you understand the read $

for pregnancy screening prior to surgery. Initial ;

FOR TESTING: (Yes to any, requires pregnancy testing, check on Anesthesia orders) © there any possibility you could be pregnant? | Are you expericncing a monthly cycle? 5 C) Are you experiencing irregular or missed cycles? Cl Tubal Ligation |

CRITERIA FOR NOT TESTING: (Yes to any, requires no pregnancy testing) Q >50 years old /no cycle for 12 months Q) Hysterectomy QO Decumented by MD there is no need

questions above and I hereby-consent tp the pregnancy testing. ?

} |a-B-an | 0 [A

Date

i I have read this and understand the potential effects anesthosia can have on a fetus. I have answered truthfully the | | !

I have read this and understand the potential effects anesthesia can have on a fetus. Ihave answered truthfully the questions above. There is no possibility I am pregnant and.I refuse to be tested for pregnancy. I understand if ] am found later to be pregnant, I release The Medical Center and Anesthesia Associates from all liability for injury to the) fetus,
